# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
The Technology of Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG)

Building a Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG) application involves a sophisticated mixture of information retrieval, natural language processing, and large language models (LLMs). The core architecture revolves around three key components: the Retrieval stage, the Generation stage, and the underlying Vector Database.

Core Components and Technologies
Vector Databases and Embedding: At the heart of RAG is the vector database, which stores proprietary or domain-specific data. This data is transformed into vector embeddings using embedding models. Vector embeddings are dense numerical representations that capture semantic meaning, enabling fast and accurate retrieval.

Retrieval Stage: When a user provides a query, the retrieval stage begins. The query is also embedded, and the system searches the vector database for relevant documents or chunks. This is typically done using similarity search algorithms like cosine similarity.

Generation Stage: The generation stage combines the retrieved documents with the context of the query. An LLM then synthesizes this information to create a comprehensive, contextually relevant response. This ensures the output is grounded in the specific data, mitigating the risk of hallucinations or inaccurate information.Through the integration of these technologies, RAG provides a powerful framework for enhancing the utility and accuracy of LLMs, making them highly effective in real-world scenarios. ^6uItUKYo

How It Works
Our RAG implementation functions through several key components:

üìÑ Document Processing: Documents are processed, split into meaningful chunks, and transformed into embeddings using OpenAI's embedding models
üíæ Storage: These embeddings are stored in PostgreSQL using the BYTEA data type, alongside document metadata and user information
üîé Retrieval: When a query is submitted, it's converted to an embedding and similarity search is performed against stored document embeddings
üß† Context Building: The most relevant document chunks are assembled into a context window using custom logic that considers:
Semantic relevance scores
Document structure (headers, paragraphs, tables)
User-selected file filters
‚úçÔ∏è Response Generation: The retrieved context is sent to the language model along with the original query to generate accurate, contextually relevant responses ^558D3T1K
